{"name":"Novella 2 — Chapter 15: Quiet Corridor","type":"document","content":"# Chapter 15: Quiet Corridor\n\nJhace walked the lane one last time with the shift list under his arm and the day’s noise already drained to a hum. Steam from the soup stalls lifted and then forgot to be dramatic. The ring glyphs had the sheen of work well used; the escort board read like a sentence no one wanted to argue with. West Mouth, Center Notch, East Gate: all three maps stayed true in the rain’s aftertaste.\n\nOperation first, simple and clean. He posted Valaryn’s new slips at the clinic nook, small squares with the clinic ⭕ and a bell mark in the margin: **paid rest** and **return time** printed by icon. Brighlee handed him the tie roll and touched the caller square in passing like someone patting a good animal. Kylar followed with a dry cloth to wipe each ridged patch so a wet thumb could still trust it.\n\nThe shift list needed its own correction. He chalked the board edge and laid the plates: bell marks for windows, a ring glyph beside each to show “one hand on home” even for rest. Under the line of names, he set a narrow row of small bells that meant **return** in plates. No text. Bodies would understand.\n\nPressure lived only in time now, in the way tired people can squander a quiet by trying to fill it. The steward’s nephew stood at a distance and practiced not interfering. Mobel’s serial board on the Hall wall reflected lamplight without inviting argument. The recall placards for **L‑72 / P‑9** had been lifted hours ago; the cord now coiled in Kylar’s hands like a calm snake.\n\nJhace pressed the ridger across the shift list’s legend strip, a shallow, final bite. The teeth sang a little, then settled. He stamped the quill square top right and the clinic ⭕ bottom left where Valaryn’s slips lived. He added a small droplet plate because rain would be back, and the board had to stay honest under weather as well as eyes.\n\nTiffani arrived with a coil of spare ties over her shoulder and the look of a person who had taught a room to respect its hinge. Her hairline still held a damp that had chosen to be clean rather than cold. She took in the board with the speed of someone inventorying tools before they sleep. “Add the bell at two here,” she said, fingertip to the line where night crews forget they have bodies. He added it. She tied the top knots on the list so a wet hand later wouldn’t pull the card sideways.\n\nThey watered from the same tin without ceremony. The tin tasted like clean iron and her hand on the side of it looked steady now that the day had stopped moving. Heat moved in him like a coal set to a ring in a forge, small and definite.\n\nThey worked the list to the end. Valaryn posted three **paid rest** slips already pre‑filled for high use stations, tucked under the shift list so habit would see them. Kylar backed away, eyes finding the ridged patch and testing it with two fingers, earning himself another private nod from both of them at once. Brighlee counted back from the next bell and marked the caller post with a small square so the night crew wouldn’t invent a seam.\n\nCost came due the way it always does, as honesty. Jhace felt the day in the hinge of his right wrist where the rod had lived too often; in the calves that had learned to make a street act like a plan; in the throat that had chosen quiet and paid for it with a rasp. He pressed his thumb into the ridged patch at the lower edge of the list and let the texture answer in kind: yes, real.\n\n“Done,” he said to the board more than to her. The corridor heard it and lowered one more note, down to the hum a place makes when it can sleep with one eye open.\n\nThey walked to the small room off the clinic where maps dry and boards get wiped and people sometimes forget how to stand like workers and remember how to stand like bodies. Valaryn had left the lamp turned low, wick trimmed so it did not chatter. A clean cloth lay on the table beside the tie roll; chalk dust had powdered the frame of a board that had been corrected and then set aside to wait for morning’s eyes.\n\nThe private night for once did not need an excuse made out of tasks. The corridor had been put to bed with its bells on paper. The kits were closed. Hooks held tools that liked being where they were. He reached for words and found he didn’t want them. He put his palm to the table’s worn edge, the grain smooth as a well‑kept bar.\n\nTiffani closed the door with the same economy she used on a hinge. The latch found its seat and stayed. She came to stand across from him and set her fingers beside his on the table, not touching, close enough for both sets of knuckles to learn the temperature of the room. The lamp found the silk in the oil on her thumb, a day’s work made visible.\n\nHe had spent years being most useful at distance: bridge angle, pressline cadence, a map’s tooth. He felt the shape of that reflex try to put itself between them and chose not to let it. The choice felt like setting a brace a degree deeper and trusting the span to take it.\n\nHe looked at her. “Close?”\n\n“Stay,” she said.\n\nThe body result arrived like a tool doing what it was made to do. Her shoulders dropped two grains. The fine tremor in her hand, the one she ignores until morning coffee can claim it, stopped. His breath, which had been living too high all week, moved down and spread where it should. They were not even clever about it. They were present.\n\nHe stepped around the table without hurry. She met him halfway. Their foreheads touched before anything else. They breathed. The room decided to listen instead of watch. He set his hands where heat asked: one at the back of her neck, one at her flank, palms open, not claiming, making a home for the bones he could feel there. Her mouth found his and did not argue about sequence. The heat that had lived shelved all season climbed and arranged the room to suit itself.\n\nHe was a man built for load paths and she was a woman who could read heat and ask it to sit. They treated each other like an operation worth surviving. No words. Not many. He said her name once the way you say the name of a tool you trust because you want it to hear itself. She pressed a hand to his chest under the coat and found the rhythm she had been hearing on rods and boards for a week. It matched hers. When braking was a choice, they didn’t take the turn. When steadiness was a choice, they took that. It was work in the way work is something your body knows before your head agrees.\n\nFade belonged where it belongs. The lamp did not go out; it lowered. The world kept its edges without becoming sharp. Breath settled into the pace that makes rooms honest. The day left them through the soles of their feet into the floor, which took it the way a span takes night frost.\n\nLater, they stood again the way people do when they have remembered something important and do not want to mishandle it. He poured water; she drank; they traded the tin as if it were a form to be completed correctly.\n\n“Tomorrow,” she said, voice clean, not a promise, an inventory. “We walk the East board and fix that tooth.”\n\n“Tomorrow,” he said. He wanted to say thank you, and did, but not with speech. He wiped the chalk rim from the board’s frame with the heel of his hand and watched the dust lift, hover, then settle in a way that satisfied a part of him that had nothing to do with corridors and everything to do with surfaces that hold the right amount of quiet.\n\nHe opened the room door and they carried the low lamp back to the posting wall. The corridor had not unlearned anything while they were gone. The escort board’s ring sat at waist height, polished by palms. The three maps hung identical and still. The shift list they had posted held its small extra bells, the **return** plates reading as clearly as the **rest** slips tucked beneath.\n\nHe tied one last knot in the lower corner of the list because corners lie and he didn’t feel like being lied to on a beautiful night. He pressed the ridged patch. She did too. Their thumbs agreed.\n\nThe quiet was not empty. It had the shape of things placed correctly. Steam slept. Water found drains it had been taught. Somewhere down‑lane, a ringer checked his rope so he wouldn’t have to think about it in the morning.\n\nOn the posting wall, the shift list hung square with the **paid rest** slips tucked under its edge and small **return** bell plates added along the line of names. Lamplight sat low. Chalk dust lay along the board’s frame like snow that knows it should not melt yet. In that quiet, human breath lived lower and steadier than rain."}

{"name":"TE’Oga — Novella 2 (Compiled • Chs 1–3)","type":"document","content":"# TE’Oga — Novella 2: Standards in Motion\n\n## Compiled Edition (Chapters 1–3)\n\n— Prepared for print/export —\n\n---\n\n### Chapter 1: Narrowvale Pilot\n\nJhace comes in with the rain. Narrowvale’s three-lane choke gleams slick, flags the color of old brass slapping on their cords. Steam from kettles shelves low, the smell of onion and wet rope. He lifts the placard kit to the posting wall and sets his boot on the bottom rung of a bent ladder that doesn’t trust him. The board he needs to cover is crowded: last‑season tax notice, a chipped fish‑day prayer tile, someone’s hand‑ink arrows pointing nowhere.\n\n“Two hands,” he says, not loud, only for the crew near. Kylar anchors the rung with a shin and his palm flat. Brighlee waits at the side with the bell card and an oilcloth roll of ties.\n\nJhace measures with fingers first. Two knuckles from the bolt head, three from the seam in the stone. The Map‑as‑Set board will live here or it will die here; there’s no point being precious somewhere else. He chalks the rectangle, an honest outline that catches the spit of weather, then opens the kit.\n\nIcon plates in their slots: droplet, wedge, ring, arrows, bell marks. The Conclave stamp sits in its felt pocket, weighty as a small vise. Ridger tool wrapped in cloth, teeth fine as a fishbone comb. He checks the ink’s drag with a thumb. Viscosity good; rain won’t thin it into lies.\n\nThe steward arrives like a brass hinge grinding dry. Jall Var carries a ledger in two hands as if it is a baby that might curse. He takes in the chalk, the board, the crew. “Not text,” he says, meaning to cut the thing short. He points with the ledger’s corner. “This lane reads. We post words.”\n\n“Bell windows are color,” Brighlee murmurs, looking nowhere.\n\nJhace gives the steward the polite weight of a glance and no more. The lane is already crowding. Carts at his flank drip, mule ears flick. Vendors fold tarps, then unfold them again when the gust shifts. Authority noise rides the rain: a council runner up the back way, someone calling about a missed fee, three men rehearsing an argument so it feels practiced. The choke is hot metal without air.\n\nHe marks the first anchor. The hammer shows its clean face, and Kylar’s small breath answers each tack with a ready tie. The board goes up steady, strip by strip, not a show. Jhace steps off the ladder, calves buzzing, and wipes rain off the board with the inside of his sleeve. The kit’s latch ticks open again. He slides out the plate for the lane map and lays it to the wood.\n\nMap‑as‑Set replaces words. He sets the three arrows for the three streams of traffic in the choke: left, heavy carts; center, foot and hand‑barrows; right, return flow and runners. The arrows’ tails meet in a simple tooth that suggests the pinch point. He presses ink and pulls clean. The black sits proud without shine. Water beads gather, refuse to smudge, and roll.\n\n“Those are lines,” Jall Var says. “Not law.”\n\nJhace checks the spacing to the caller post he chalked earlier. Brighlee is already there, tying a small square to the post that announces bell windows. Blue for Four, yellow for Two, the squares clipped to spin when the wind wants them. She gives him a look that says: simple holds.\n\n“Law is posted,” Jhace says, soft. He doesn’t say it to the steward; he says it to the board. He fits the ring glyph at waist height, the one that marks the home line for hands. The ring must be obvious but not intrusive. Too high and people miss it; too low and children worry it like a toy. He measures from his belt to the board, sets the ring, inked and honest.\n\nThe wedge glyph sits where it must sit, upstream of a Veil zone that will arrive in two chapters’ worth of work for other people. For now, the wedge simply points to the corner turn standard ahead, a promise the board makes and the crews must keep. He places the wedge and pulls the plate. Clean edge, no feathering. Rain tracks around it like water around a polished stone.\n\nJall Var is not done. “Without text, my clerks must interpret. You invite mishandling. Fines fall wrong. You will cause mistakes.” A vendor nearby, hearing fines, goes quiet. The rain doesn’t.\n\nKylar keeps his hands busy at the ties, learning the icons by touch as he has been taught: arrow is a long bone, wedge is a tooth, ring is a smooth coin, droplet is a tear that points down to where oils belong. Jhace approves the habit by not stopping it. He sets the bell marks in a neat row along the board’s bottom edge, two short stripes, one long, for the cadence that will regulate changes. He hears the future taps in his bones, a steadying thought in the weather’s noise.\n\nHe drifts the ridger out of its cloth and holds it near the bottom right of the card. Tempermark isn’t the ritual today, but a ridge at the legend will keep counterfeits from slipping in early. He presses the teeth with a palm heel until they bite a relief into the inked field. Not a flourish, just a fact you can feel.\n\n“Your people can leave the words to the court?” Jall Var asks, voice climbing. “We are literate. We will not be reduced.”\n\nJhace’s voice is tired from the morning’s pressline run across Grindheim’s span. It comes out hoarse, the way a hinge sounds after salt air. “The corridor reads the icons,” he says. “Clerks can read as much as they like elsewhere.” He lifts the Conclave stamp and sets it under the wedge. The stamp’s face is a small square with the quill mark. He inks it and presses until the wood says yes with a small change in tone. When he pulls away, the black square sits like a seal on a crate. Lawful enough for any steward who bothers to look.\n\n“Who signed that?” Jall Var asks.\n\n“Corlexi,” Brighlee answers, because she was there. She taps the ledger strip that lives in her roll where the approval number sits dry and precise. She doesn’t offer it to the steward. Rain and paper are enemies; this crowd will see it later when it can be seen.\n\nThe choke flexes. A mule pushes its shoulder into the wrong lane. Jhace steps into the center without fanfare, one palm out for gentle stop, one finger to the new map, then a pivot of the wrist that returns the animal to left flow. He doesn’t shout. He doesn’t need to. The driver reads the arrows and yields. Rain runs off the brim of the man’s hat and finds its way to the gutters instead of down the corridor’s spine.\n\nPressure builds again at the back as a cart’s wheel catches on a loose cobble. The sound is a dull metal waver. Jhace feels his calves complain as he half‑crouches to reset the stone with his foot and a pry of the hammer’s handle. Kylar is there with a wedge of wood to keep the repair honest. They don’t exchange words. The work is a unit of actions that fit without comment.\n\n“Card needs warnings,” the steward says, raising his voice to cover the crowd. “Words about penalties. Words about exceptions.” He enjoys the shape of exceptions.\n\nJhace sets the final icon: the droplet. A small mark at the board’s lower left that directs oil use to the annex and keeps the corridor free of false cures. Salee will love it when she sees it. He cleans the plate on the cloth’s dry edge and racks it home. Cost shows in the small shake at his wrist as he unwinds from the ladder one more time. He is thirsty. He is nearly done.\n\nHe steps back until his shoulders touch the posting wall. Brighlee lifts the caller square and flicks Blue to face the lane. “Bell Four weather,” she says, low, so the world can arrange itself. She ties it off with a knot that can be changed with wet fingers. Kylar rechecks the ties in sequence, then palms the ring glyph to test its height, an apprentice ritual they made up in a dry moment and kept.\n\nJall Var opens his mouth, maybe to announce a stay. A gust blows his ledger’s pages into his face, and he takes a small step back. The crowd laughs, the soft kind that makes the temperature of a place rise half a degree.\n\nJhace takes the moment. He lifts the ridger once more and bites a thin ridge along the legend line, the place where a thumb will go if the eyes don’t trust yet. He breathes the way he teaches: in for four, out for six. The breath burns at the top of his chest where the morning left a rasp. He can feel the ache ripening in his calves, a clean soreness like metal cooling right.\n\n“Post is live,” he says to the board. To the lane. Not to the steward. He puts the ridger away, seals the kit, and lets the tools rest.\n\nBehavior changes first at the edges. A barrower reaches the choke and pauses, uncertain, then sees his lane in the arrow and steps into it without being told. A boy with a coil of cord at his waist drifts his hand to the ring glyph as he walks and smiles like something fit in his head without pain. To the right, a pair of runners align themselves and stop fighting space they do not own.\n\nThe steward tries one last time. “If someone asks, where do they read the clause?”\n\nJhace tips his chin at the Conclave square. “There,” he says. “The clause is that this is the clause.” He doesn’t wait for the answer. He turns to the board and rubs the lower corner with the pad of his thumb to see if the ridge holds under rain and flesh. It does.\n\nBrighlee unrolls a small strip with the caller symbol and slips it over the post so the next crew knows where to stand and when. Kylar moves through the first three carts like he was born a knot‑opener, touching nothing, only pointing. A mule snorts, a wheel creaks, steam lifts. Air finds a path again. The corridor’s tone drops half a note.\n\nJhace steps away, hoarseness a scratch that won’t drink water until the work is fully done. He lets the lane show him if it learned something. It did. He feels it in the way the pressure at the choke goes from thrust to glide.\n\nHe sets the stamp again just once, a second bite beside the first, not required, only present for the people who count such things. Then he does the last check: he runs his own thumb over the little Tempermark ridge where the legend lives, skin finding the raised line by instinct rather than sight.\n\nA woman with a market cart does the same, tentative, then sure. Her thumb finds the ridge. The cart eases forward without a shouted order.\n\n---\n\n### Chapter 2: South Annex Veils\n\nTiffani had the benches warm and the lamps turned down to a honey dim so the glass would tell the truth. The South Clinic Annex breathed its own weather: oil smell, thread kits lined like small bones, veils stacked in rolls that caught the light at their edges. She chalked the wedge glyph on the teaching board, angled toward the corner work, and set the metronome bell two beats soft.\n\nThe hot racks arrived off schedule, metal shrieking against metal. A runner and his partner came shouldering through the Annex arch with the first frame still giving off heat. Steam lifted when rain from their coats met the rack’s bars. Salee swore in the doorway, one clipped syllable, then claimed the oil shelf from a curious trainee with a wrist tap that was gentle and absolute.\n\n“Wedge before Veil,” Tiffani said. She kept her voice low and clean, the way you speak beside reactive material. “Corners three‑count. We practice with dead panes first.” She nodded toward the practice frames, the ones with score marks to show where old failures began.\n\nKylar stood at the edge with a coil of ties he didn’t need for this class but didn’t put down because hands need a task. Valaryn, sleeves rolled, laid out return‑to‑work slips where trainees could see them and not touch. Tiffani let their competence be background muscle. The work in front of her was three apprentices new to Annex discipline and one old hand who had learned in a shop with more shouting than standard.\n\n... (chapter continues in full as posted in the canvas for Chapter 2) ...\n\n---\n\n### Chapter 3: Pressline Cadence\n\nJhace reached the Narrowvale choke ahead of the bell change and found the weather already doing the work of a poor foreman. Rain hit in sheets that turned cobbles to polished iron. Kettle steam bent under the gusts and laid a low fog at shin height. The lane held like a frayed rope in a hand that hadn’t decided to let go or pull. Bell Two’s window was about to end; Bell Four would raise its face. That seam was where lanes came apart.\n\nHe slung the short bar across his shoulder. It was nothing more than a length of tempered rod with a coin‑thick cap for the taps. The pressline lives in small, clear sounds. He kept the placard kit under his cloak to keep the ridger teeth dry. Brighlee stood already at the caller post, Blue square still showing, fingers at the tie knot, eyes on him. Kylar held a coil of cord and the little hammer like a young man who had understood that hands idle at a choke were a liability.\n\n... ## A) Confirm you understand the rails (YES/NO with one-line paraphrase each)
1) POV: Only Jhace or Tiffani, tight third, one POV per scene. Interludes ≤120 words, no interiority.

4) Sound stance: keep existing manuscript phrasing; **no new musical metaphors**; prefer mechanical/material cues (whine/hiss/ring/even/level/pulse/pressure).  
5) Romance/consent: one explicit yes/stop line + immediate body result; no commentary.  
6) Thermal Mains: background only; never accessed or theorized.

### Rails — Confirmed
1) POV: YES — Only Jhace or Tiffani in tight third; one POV per scene; interludes ≤120 words with zero interiority.  
2) Chapter contract: YES — Action on-page by ≤250 words; closing within ≤200 words after operation; end on a public artifact + one concrete image; no ledger-style headings in prose.  
3) HALT: YES — Exactly one HALT in the book; it posts and is cleared same day with setter witness.  
4) Sound stance: YES — Preserve manuscript phrasing; avoid new musical metaphors; use mechanical/material cues (whine/hiss/ring/level/pressure).  
5) Romance/consent: YES — One explicit yes/stop line followed by immediate physical result; no narration about it.  
6) Thermal Mains: YES — Background only; never accessed or hypothesized.  
7) Brighlee mode: YES — Per scene, either pure function (clip/post/“Posted.”) or a single micro human beat, not both.

### My Issues — Your Fix-in-a-Line
- Inventory intros → Start with a physical action or placement; push lists after the first kinetic beat or collapse into working nouns.  
- Aphorisms → Delete slogan lines; replace with concrete cause→effect shown on bodies, tools, and posted results.  
- Ledger bleed → Remove colon labels and audit diction; render artifacts in-scene and reserve formal fields for posted cards only.  
- Repeat choreography → If a sequence repeats, compress to one clean cycle and vary surface (material, angle, weather) or elide with a single precise line.  
- POV creep → Strip side-character thoughts; keep them to observable action, brief speech, or posted outcomes.  
- Music lexicon → Swap melody/chorus/rhythm for cadence in taps only; prefer mechanical verbs and sensorics (tap, ring, pitch, load).  
- Over-explaining → After the board is shown, cut commentary; one proof action or crowd behavior is the explanation.  
- Overlong open/close → Trim preamble to first on-page move; cap endings at artifact + image within 200 words.

### Methods — How You’ll Police Yourself
1) Chapter boundary detection: Use TOC cues and search for “Chapter” + numerals/words; if a Prologue exists, Chapter 1 starts at the first header matching `/^Chapter\\s*1\\b/i` or the first scene with Jhace/Tiffani POV and Map-as-Set pilot beats. Cross-check end by locating the artifact+image clause for that beat.  
2) Heuristics:  
   - Inventory intros: `/^(Kit|Bench|Board|Crate|Tools)\\b.*[,;].*(,|;).*/` in first 4 lines.  
   - Aphorisms: `/\\b(is|are|was)\\b.*\\b(truth|trust|standard|city|corridor)\\b(\\s+.*)?\\.$/` or quotes-as-maxims.  
   - Ledger bleed: `/^[A-Z][a-z]+\\s*:\\s/` or “Public artifact:”/“Posted:” in narrative.  
   - Musical metaphors: `/melody|chorus|symphony|harmony|songlike|tempo(?!\\s*bars)/i`.  
   - Repeat choreography: co-occurrence window with `/Map-as-Set|red slash|quarantine cord|caller windows|ridged patch|tap tap/` repeated twice within ~300 words.  
3) Compression algorithm:  
   1) Flag non-action sentences before the first kinetic verb; cut or fold into the first move.  
   2) Collapse duplicate sequences to one instance; retain one proof beat and one crowd response.  
   3) Replace abstract lines with concrete sensory or posted outcomes; delete restatement.  
   4) Prune modifiers and parallelisms; keep one strongest material cue per sentence.  
   5) Audit closing 250 words; ensure artifact+image lands, then cut any tail past the image.  
4) Cost callbacks:  
   - calf ache  
   - hoarse voice  
   - wrist throb  
   - jaw tight  
   - eye strain  
   - shoulder burn  
   - salt on tongue  
   - fray band pale  
5) Acceptance tests (PASS/FAIL):  
   - Action by ≤250 words  
   - Ends on artifact + single image; no ledger headings  
   - Aphorism-free; replace with cause→effect  
   - Sound mechanical/material; no new musical metaphors  
   - Single-POV interiority only  
   - Close ≤200 words post operation  
   - Brighlee mode consistent (functional OR one-beat)

### Commitment
“I will not rewrite until you supply the manuscript and the edit prompt. When you paste them, I will return **only the tightened Chapter 1** with a change log and a private continuity note. I will proceed to Chapter 2 only when you say so.”

# SURGICAL EDITOR PROMPT — “Standards in Motion” (Return Chapter 1 Only)

You are performing a **chapter-by-chapter compression and polish pass** on the complete novella manuscript **Standards in Motion** (Novella 2 in the Te’Oga cycle). You will be given the **full manuscript text** as input right now. From that single input, you must output **only the revised Chapter 1** in this turn, following the rules below.

- Output **Chapter 1 (tightened)** immediately. You will handle later chapters only when asked (e.g., “Proceed to Chapter 2”).

- Veinwork moves: Trace, Set, Bridge, Pressline, Tempermark, Bind (micro), Countermark (cooler than birth), Lume, Veil, Slake, Annealshift, Thread, Map-as-Set.
